  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c8709995-a1aa-4fdf-8106-abb85eb4d962'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText11997957713808431402" style="display:none"><div>This irresistible first novel tells the story of a quiet boy who embarks on a dangerous quest in order to fulfill his destiny—and find his father—in a strange world beneath New York City.<br /><br />When Gregor falls through a grate in the laundry room of his apartment building, he hurtles into the dark Underland, where spiders, rats, cockroaches coexist uneasily with humans. This world is on the brink of war, and Gregor's arrival is no accident. A prophecy foretells that Gregor has a role to play in the Underland's uncertain future. Gregor wants no part of it -- until he realizes it's the only way to solve the mystery of his father's disappearance. Reluctantly, Gregor embarks on a dangerous adventure that will change both him and the Underland forever.</div></span>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/33430429-c-wilhoit"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/33430429-c-wilhoit">C. Wilhoit</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This series is better than the Hunger Games and I have no clue why it doesn't get more attention. Probably because it would be pretty much impossible <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This series is better than the Hunger Games and I have no clue why it doesn't get more attention. Probably because it would be pretty much impossible to make into a movie with one of the main characters being a toddler. It's up there with Harry Potter for me. Very intense. By the last book or two it's not a children's book anymore to me- you're getting into adult territory with war and serious themes, but you won't be able to stop reading. Also great on audiobook- the narrator does a great job and adds a lot to it. Question- does anyone else think that the phrase "everyone a rager" in Lorde's song Glory and Gore might refer to this series?<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_120950949" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/120950949" />
    <a title="Eh?Eh!" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/137273-eh-eh"><img alt="Eh?Eh!" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370013095p2/137273.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/120950949?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eh?Eh!" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eh?Eh!" href="/user/show/137273-eh-eh">Eh?Eh!</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/137273-eh-eh?shelf=babble-added">babble-added</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/137273-eh-eh?shelf=goodreaders-made-me">goodreaders-made-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120950949" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12152950074437919378">I recently went solo dining with the 2nd book in the series and sat down at a counter, speeding through the large font and well-spaced text. The restaurant started to fill up and another solo diner sat down next to me. I glanced over at his magazine and saw that it was a scientific journal open to an article about the brain. I casually angled the cover of my Scholastic-published book away from his view and kept reading, very self-conscious of the approximately 18 grades of school between our rea</span>
  <span id="freeText12152950074437919378" style="display:none">I recently went solo dining with the 2nd book in the series and sat down at a counter, speeding through the large font and well-spaced text. The restaurant started to fill up and another solo diner sat down next to me. I glanced over at his magazine and saw that it was a scientific journal open to an article about the brain. I casually angled the cover of my Scholastic-published book away from his view and kept reading, very self-conscious of the approximately 18 grades of school between our reading materials.<br /><br />Sigh.<br /><br />I'm bouncing around in my reading material lately. I've been trying to force the weighter books and it's like an overtight pair of jeans. Lay back on the bed, take a deep breath, and hope you can wrestle that zipper up before the oxygen runs out or the button pops off and you lose an eye. The YA and younger books are more like comfortable sweatpants, the waistband slightly stretched and the material over the seat taking on a sheen from wear. I need to take in a few sweatpants books before attempting another jeans book. Who am I trying to impress? No need to do the David Hasselhoff on <i>Baywatch</i> stomach suck.<br /><br />This is what I repeat to myself when I sit next to someone reading a scientific journal open to an article about the brain...you couldn't sit somewhere else, brain guy???<br /><br />The beginning of the 2nd book helped me pinpoint why I liked this 1st book so much. With the next in the series, Gregor is suddenly having these abilities he never had before. Booooo. The first book moved forward with his own average self, no special powers needed. While he may have been written as more selfless than the typical boy his age, he made mistakes and was cranky like a real boy. When he was courageous, loyal, loving, or expressed empathy, it wasn't unusual - it could be duplicated by any child who read this book. The value of that! You too can be like this!:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>[Gregor]* nodded. He could never hate people very long because he always ended up finding out something sad about them that he had to factor in. Like this kid at school everybody hated because he was always pushing little kids around and then one day they found out his dad had hit him so much, he was in the hospital. With stuff like that, all Gregor could feel was bad.</i>
</blockquote><br />Wonderful.<br /><br />Oh, the story was set in this quest for his father with a fantastic imaginary world underground featuring people who had lived there so long that they were pale-haired, translucent-skinned, and violet-eyed. The allies and enemies were gigantic bats, cockroaches, and rats. This is meant for a younger audience than <i>The Hunger Games</i> trilogy, so probably elementary age. The quest kicked off with an awful set of prophetic verse (not as bad as Brian "One Trick Pony" Jacques but nowhere near the soaring glory (to me) of Susan Cooper). The ending was rushed. But I loved it for keeping the hero ordinary.<br /><br />My favorite line? From my favorite character, the little sister, Boots: "I poop!"<br /><br /><br /><br />*Lookie! The square brackets don't insert a colon anymore!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12152950074437919378" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer80062921" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3456135766557109540">so this is how superweak my life is: on friday i rushed home from work in the rain to get some homework done. whee... but then i ended up writing that wuthering heights review, inspired by the rain and the clouds etc. and i did some work, but not a ton. and i thought to myself, what do i really want to be doing? and the answer was - put on my pajamas, eat peanut butter pretzels and read unchallenging children's books. so i did. and you can all suck it, with your parties and balls and galas. 'cuz</span>
  <span id="freeText3456135766557109540" style="display:none">so this is how superweak my life is: on friday i rushed home from work in the rain to get some homework done. whee... but then i ended up writing that wuthering heights review, inspired by the rain and the clouds etc. and i did some work, but not a ton. and i thought to myself, what do i really want to be doing? and the answer was - put on my pajamas, eat peanut butter pretzels and read unchallenging children's books. so i did. and you can all suck it, with your parties and balls and galas. 'cuz i had myself a nice time.<br><br>i didn't like it as much as the hunger games; which is teen fiction, not juvie, so maybe i'm not as developmentally stunted as i thought. look, i'm growing up before your eyes! she has a real knack for pacing, which is way more important in children's literature than adult, just because of attention-span, particularly now, when the options for children are increasingly electronic and faster-paced - a book really has to capture the imagination in order to hold a child's attention, and i think this does a good job of that. i also appreciate her very low emphasis on sentimentality. it is less pronounced than in the hunger games, because of the younger audience, but it's an adventure book, life's hard, things die. and i think that's a good element in children's literature; her lack of prettifying realities. i will probably read the other books in the series, providing my social life doesn't improve, but i don't feel the same urgency to read them that i do for the teen series. it may be the subject matter/younger audience thing, or the lack of a true "cliffhanger" at the end of the book, but i probably will get to them. it was enjoyable, and if you have children, you should probably pick these up and pretend you are reading them together because your kids enjoy them.<br><br>and now i can give greg back his copy, and that gets one more book out of my house. which means there's room for one more book, basically. this is how the problem exacerbates...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>

<div id="review_35739997" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/35739997" />
    <a title="Rfrancik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1574297-rfrancik"><img alt="Rfrancik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1224964501p2/1574297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/35739997?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rfrancik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rfrancik" href="/user/show/1574297-rfrancik">Rfrancik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1574297-rfrancik?shelf=6-fictional-chapter-books">6-fictional-chapter-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1574297-rfrancik?shelf=1-e">1-e</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer35739997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1651712809299943798">When Gregor falls after his little sister down the laundry shoot he finds himself in a new land. He is faced with deciding where to place his loyalties, how to survive and given the opportunity to search for his father who unaccountably disappeared 2 years ago. <br/><br/>This book has ruined my entire day! I have laundry to fold, dinner to cook, breakfast to eat, 3 papers to write and lesson plans to develop. Instead, I've spent my morning snuggled under a down quilt devouring Gregor the Overlander. As so</span>
  <span id="freeText1651712809299943798" style="display:none">When Gregor falls after his little sister down the laundry shoot he finds himself in a new land. He is faced with deciding where to place his loyalties, how to survive and given the opportunity to search for his father who unaccountably disappeared 2 years ago. <br /><br />This book has ruined my entire day! I have laundry to fold, dinner to cook, breakfast to eat, 3 papers to write and lesson plans to develop. Instead, I've spent my morning snuggled under a down quilt devouring Gregor the Overlander. As soon as I finished it I slid into my car and ran back to work to collect the next four books in the series. It looks like the rest of my life is going on hold for awhile. Good-by responsibiliy, Good-by family, HELLO UNDERLANDERS!<br /><br />I have always loved fairytales and mysteries in the Agatha Christie model. It's restful and reassuring to know there may be trials and tribulations but good will always defeat evil and the deserving will live happily ever after.<br /><br />Gregor the Overlander carries these themes forward but provides subtle opportunities for the reader to question their convictions about "right and wrong" through the protagonist's encounters with various species in the Underworld. Equally appealing is the sharing of Gregor's thoughts as he begins to recognize the limits he has set for himself with self imposed rules after his father's disappearance. <br /><br />So often books of this genre for the elementary crowd become preachy and moralistic. Suzanne Collins does not preach. She invites the reader to explore issues about tolerance, responsibility, growing up, and loyalty for themselves. This first book is the equal of the Harry Potter books exploring the same issues with an emotional power and linguistic accessablity for the 5th-8th grade crowd. I've listed a few of my favorite quotes below. <br /><br />1) .."And then there was Tick. Brave little Tick who had flown into the face of an army of rats to save his baby sister. Tick--who never spoke much. Tick--who shared her food. Tick--who was after all just a roach. Just a roach who had given all the time she had left so that Boots could have more. ...Somehow Tick's sacrifice had crushed whatever thin shell remained between him and sorrow. From now on he felt an allegiance to the roaches he knew would never fade."<br /><br />2) "Well, Boot's courage might only count when she could count, but her ability to love counted all the time."<br /><br />3) "No one who spends years with the rats can expect to be unchanged....but will his mind and body heal, I believe so."<br /><br />4) "He was done with the rule now. For good. Even if times got bad he would never again deny himself the possibility that the future might be happy even if the present was painful. He would allow himself dreams."<br /><br />Because I teach in a school where far too many children have parents and siblings in jail, I intend to use this book as one of a collection about children who overcome the odds to determine their own destiny.<br /><br />Reviews: <br /><br />1) Booklist starred (November 15, 2003 (Vol. 100, No. 6)) Recommends for gr. 4-7 and states.."Collins creates a fascinating, vivid, highly original world and a superb story to go along with it. ..This is sure to be a solid hit with young fantasy fans.<br /><br />2) Horn Book starred (Spring 2004) writes "Collins sends a reluctant Gregor on the classic hero's journey in this fast-paced, immensely satisfying narrative."<br /><br />Both of these reviews would incline me towards the book's purchase. Several of the other reviews also mention it is one of a series and they all recommend it for the same age groups. What the reviewers fail to say is now much parents would enjoy sharing this book with their children.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1651712809299943798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_45528518" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45528518" />
    <a title="Meredith Holley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1302775-meredith-holley"><img alt="Meredith Holley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548641865p2/1302775.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45528518?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith Holley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith Holley" href="/user/show/1302775-meredith-holley">Meredith Holley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">School Teachers and Librarians</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=young-reader">young-reader</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=do-not-judge-by-the-cover">do-not-judge-by-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=classic-young-reader">classic-young-reader</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45528518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9984282396911247965">The covers of the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/262430.Gregor_the_Overlander__The_Underland_Chronicles_Book_One_' title='Gregor the Overlander (The Underland Chronicles Book One) by Suzanne Collins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Underland Chronicles</a> do them no end of disservice. Since my policy is to judge a book by its cover, it took reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games' title='The Hunger Games by Suzanne Collins' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hunger Games</a> to convince me to pick them up. I had always assumed they would be machine generated chapter books with mythical creatures protecting or seeking some ring or sword, or who knows what, that has some symbolic meaning - or doesn't. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/153394.Suzanne_Collins' title='Suzanne Collins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Suzanne Collins</a>, however, is in no way machine-generated. She is <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3356.Fyodor_Dostoevsky' title='Fyodor Dostoevsky' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dostoyevski</a> for the young-reader crowd. While she uses </span>
  <span id="freeText9984282396911247965" style="display:none">The covers of the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/262430.Gregor_the_Overlander__The_Underland_Chronicles_Book_One_" title="Gregor the Overlander (The Underland Chronicles Book One) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">Underland Chronicles</a> do them no end of disservice. Since my policy is to judge a book by its cover, it took reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games" title="The Hunger Games by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a> to convince me to pick them up. I had always assumed they would be machine generated chapter books with mythical creatures protecting or seeking some ring or sword, or who knows what, that has some symbolic meaning - or doesn't. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/153394.Suzanne_Collins" title="Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">Suzanne Collins</a>, however, is in no way machine-generated. She is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3356.Fyodor_Dostoevsky" title="Fyodor Dostoevsky" rel="nofollow noopener">Dostoyevski</a> for the young-reader crowd. While she uses the quest trope in each of the Underland stories, her reflections of politics and international history are both gentle and unflinchingly horrifying. Kids have to learn about genocide somehow . . . I guess.<br /><br />In comparison to other popular child-soldier (or children-save-the-world) stories, the Underland Chronicles are not comforting in the way <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3.Harry_Potter_and_the_Sorcerer_s_Stone__Harry_Potter___1_" title="Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone (Harry Potter, #1) by J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a> are, nor are they as morally-outraged and uncomfortable as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/375802.Ender_s_Game__Ender_s_Saga___1_" title="Ender's Game (Ender's Saga, #1) by Orson Scott Card" rel="nofollow noopener">Ender's Game</a>, but I found them more honest than all of those. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/153394.Suzanne_Collins" title="Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">Collins</a> never seems overcome by her own power as an author, self-indulgent in her story-telling, or worried that her audience won't understand her overall message. That may be the mark of a good editing team, and if so, A+ to them. Her writing is not as lyrically beautiful as Kate DiCamillo's (whose is, for that matter?), but, like Dostoyevski's, it is very effective in reflecting doubts about human nature and, at times, touching. It makes me wish, once again, that Dostoyevski was able to edit well. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9984282396911247965" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6542201947600278070" style="display:none">Gregor the Overlander (Underland Chronicles, #1), Suzanne Collins<br />The Underland Chronicles is a series of five epic fantasy novels by Suzanne Collins, first published between 2003 and 2007. It tells the story of a boy named Gregor and his adventures in the "Underland", a subterranean world located under New York City. The Underland is inhabited by humans who traveled below hundreds of years ago, along with various giant versions of creatures like bats, cockroaches, and rats. According to the author, the series involves many topics relating to war, including biological warfare, genocide, and military intelligence. While not as well known as the author's subsequent Hunger Games trilogy, it has been reviewed favorably by many critics.<br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: پنجم ماه جولای سال 2013 میلادی<br />عنوان: تاریخ اعماق زمین - کتاب 1 - سفر شگفت انگیز گریگور؛ نویسنده: سوزان کالینز؛ مترجم: عاطفه احمدی؛ تهران، ویدا، چاپ اول و دوم 1391؛ در 268 ص؛ شابک: 9786002910172؛ چاپ سوم و چهارم 1392؛ موضوع: داستانهای علمی تخیلی از نویسندگان انگلیسی قرن 20 م<br />نقل از متن: گریگور تکه‌ ای یخ از فریزر برداشت، آن را روی صورتش کشید و زل زد به حیاط؛ سگ ولگردی دوروبر سطل زباله‌ ای که تا کله پرُ بود، بو می‌کشید. سگ پنجه‌ هایش را روی لبۀ‌ سطل گذاشته و کجش کرده بود و زباله‌ ها را وسط پیاده‌ رو می‌ریخت. نگاه گریگور به چند شکل سایه‌ مانند افتاد که با سرعت کنار دیوار وول می‌خوردند و این‌طرف و آن‌طرف می­رفتند؛ موش‌ها. او هیچ‌ وقت درست و حسابی به‌شان عادت نکرده بود. برخلاف همیشه، این‌بار هیچ‌کس در حیاط نبود. بیشتر وقت‌ها آن‌جا پر بود از بچه‌ هایی که توپ‌ بازی می‌کردند، از روی طناب می‌پریدند، یا روی میله‌ های بازی کهنه تاب می‌خوردند؛ اما امروز صبح، همۀ بچه‌ های چهار تا چهارده‌ ساله با اتوبوسی به اردو رفته بودند، همه به جز یک نفر. پایان نقل. ا. شربیانی</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1327972142" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14503997874675183930">I want to give this book so many more than 5 stars. It was SO SO FREAKING GOOD!!! (I pressed the exclamation mark on my phone really hard then just for extra emphasis) :)<br/><br/>Being a book that is intended for younger readers than me, I thought this would just be a fun little read. However in all honesty it had me gripped from beginning to end. <br/><br/>I loved the characters. They had so much more depth than I expected them to. I mean Gregor is an 11 year old kid who has been kind of been forced to be the man</span>
  <span id="freeText14503997874675183930" style="display:none">I want to give this book so many more than 5 stars. It was SO SO FREAKING GOOD!!! (I pressed the exclamation mark on my phone really hard then just for extra emphasis) :)<br /><br />Being a book that is intended for younger readers than me, I thought this would just be a fun little read. However in all honesty it had me gripped from beginning to end. <br /><br />I loved the characters. They had so much more depth than I expected them to. I mean Gregor is an 11 year old kid who has been kind of been forced to be the man of the house after his dad disappeared mysteriously 2 years ago. He doesn't let himself dream about happy times because he is struggling to actually be happy with his family not whole. Bro, you're breaking my heart :( Then there is his 2 year old sister Boots (a nickname) who adds so much to the book with her innocence. She kind of reminds me of Sunny Baudelaire from A Series of Unfortunate Events because she is so adorable and obviously isn't speaking properly yet, but she is integral to the team and actually helps bring them all together.<br /><br />Then there are all the giant animals and they are so cool, you can't help but care about them. Even the bugs. This isn't a spoiler particularly because the prophecy says that 4 of the group of 12 will die, but when one of them does I actually had to stop reading. I sat there in stunned silence and mourned the loss of a freaking bug. <br /><br />Some of the other things I loved are:<br />- the world because it's underground and I like the idea of an underground community<br />- the relationship between humans and animals. I'm an animal lover so I really appreciated that. <br />- a mysterious prophecy. I really like seeing prophecies unfold in books. <br />- the fact that it actually surprised me with some of the things that happen. I sometimes find it easy to see what is gonna happen but not this time<br />- and how addictive and action packed it is.<br /><br />Chances are you have read The Hunger Games by Suzanne Collins too, and if you like her writing and like fast paced books (and you like middle grade books) then you should definitely try this. I implore you because it needs more hype!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14503997874675183930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_88587975" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/88587975" />
    <a title="Laurel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/957217-laurel"><img alt="Laurel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576972516p2/957217.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/88587975?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurel" href="/user/show/957217-laurel">Laurel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780307283375" href="/book/show/262431.Gregor_the_Overlander">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/957217-laurel?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/957217-laurel?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/957217-laurel?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer88587975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12321922639659697826">With a few exceptions, I am not typically a big fan of science fiction/fantasy, nor of bugs and rats and dark places. Had I not read and loved <u>The Hunger Games,</u> I never would have even considered reading this book. And I would have most certainly been missing out.<br/><br/>This is Suzanne Collins' first novel, and it is quite a first novel. <u>Gregor the Overlander</u> centers around an eleven-year-old boy and his little sister who fall through a grate in the laundry room of their apartment complex. After being </span>
  <span id="freeText12321922639659697826" style="display:none">With a few exceptions, I am not typically a big fan of science fiction/fantasy, nor of bugs and rats and dark places. Had I not read and loved <u>The Hunger Games,</u> I never would have even considered reading this book. And I would have most certainly been missing out.<br /><br />This is Suzanne Collins' first novel, and it is quite a first novel. <u>Gregor the Overlander</u> centers around an eleven-year-old boy and his little sister who fall through a grate in the laundry room of their apartment complex. After being hurtled down a long tunnel, they find themselves in the midst of a strange Underland full of talking giant cockroaches, rats, bats and spiders, as well as humans with translucent skin and violet eyes. As the children become acquainted with the strange beings and history of this mysterious land, a prophetic quest forms to find Gregor's long lost father (believed to have fallen victim to some of the creatures here years earlier), and lots of adventure ensues.<br /><br />Apparently, the author was inspired to write this book after wondering what <u>Alice and Wonderland</u> may have been like had it taken place in a city, where one is more likely to fall down a manhole than a bunny hole. <br /><br />I thought it was a fantastic story; a real page turner that, amidst all the adventure, asks its reader to consider issues of friendship, responsibility, tolerance, acceptance, determination and loyalty. Very imaginative and well written. I highly recommend it, particularly if you enjoy YA fantasy or loved <u> The Hunger Games</u>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12321922639659697826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_690135097" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/690135097" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/690135097?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=magical-fantasy">magical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-male-narrators">ya-male-narrators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer690135097" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16746496904839022078"><b>Well that was sufficiently fantastic.</b> I, naturally, am a HUGE <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_' title='The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hunger Games</a> fan and basically wanted to read this because SUZANNE COLLINS. Obviously my brain had a lot of pressure on this book aaaand...it's <i>very</i> different (obviously) from THG. It's middle-grade. It's an adventure with prophecies and talking animals. And I really enjoyed it!<br/><br/><b>The characters were <i>adorable</i>. </b>The main character is Gregor (DUH) and he's a fabulous older brother, but he's not perfect. At the same time, though, he didn</span>
  <span id="freeText16746496904839022078" style="display:none"><b>Well that was sufficiently fantastic.</b> I, naturally, am a HUGE <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a> fan and basically wanted to read this because SUZANNE COLLINS. Obviously my brain had a lot of pressure on this book aaaand...it's <i>very</i> different (obviously) from THG. It's middle-grade. It's an adventure with prophecies and talking animals. And I really enjoyed it!<br /><br /><b>The characters were <i>adorable</i>. </b>The main character is Gregor (DUH) and he's a fabulous older brother, but he's not perfect. At the same time, though, he didn't make a bucket-load of dumb decisions which I'm SO grateful for. I really hate stupid decisions. Ergh. But Gregory was really smart and logical, and had a bit of sass, and he wouldn't leave his little sister EVER. Which leads me to the cutest human in the universe: Boots! (Well, her real name is Margaret, but who's going to call her that?! HA. BOOTS IS SO CUTE.) She's the most friendly loveable little kid in the world. And her mannerisms and speech were so totally spot on for being a two-year-old. I read a lot of books and often feel the babies aren't...well...realistic. But Boots is SO realistic. (Trust me, I just spent the morning with my 2yrs niece and then read this in the afternoon. 100% of realism to Boots. A cookie will basically fix everything.) I was just so completely in love with Boots and I thought Gregor was terrific.<br /><br />So my only problem was:<b>I couldn't care less about the animals.</b> Call me a hater (actually, um, don't) BUT I HATE BUGS. I FREAKING HATE RATS AND BATS AND BUGS. So when they died (and applause for MG books that kill things/people/whatever) I just was like "Oh so what?" Which is, um, heartless of me. <br />But they're <i>bugs</i>. Ugh.<br /><br />Although is it just me or is the good-rat Ripred like another version of Haymitch?!! Snarky and wise. I SEE WHAT YOU DID THERE, SUZANNE COLLINS. (Although, um, I know, these books came first, but shhh, don't ruin my cacophonies.) <br /><br /><b>Anyway, this was fantastic and I want to read the rest of the series ASAP!</b> </span>
  <a data-text-id="16746496904839022078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17157148470064075882">Even though this book has nothing really to do with Kafka, I can't get it out of my head that somewhere in this series is some of the weird Jew from Prague. The cover looks sort of Prague like. There is a main character named Gregor, and there are giant fucking cockroaches in it (must I swear in every children's review I write?). <br/><br/>There has been no real Kafka in the book though. There are some Daddy issues but Kafka doesn't hold the patent on that. Besides looking for Kafka though, I found this f</span>
  <span id="freeText17157148470064075882" style="display:none">Even though this book has nothing really to do with Kafka, I can't get it out of my head that somewhere in this series is some of the weird Jew from Prague. The cover looks sort of Prague like. There is a main character named Gregor, and there are giant fucking cockroaches in it (must I swear in every children's review I write?). <br /><br />There has been no real Kafka in the book though. There are some Daddy issues but Kafka doesn't hold the patent on that. Besides looking for Kafka though, I found this fun. Apparently my view of fun lately is fantastical adventures children go on that I can read in a couple of hours. I'm either regressing, or just making up for all the books I never read as a little kid. <br /><br />But I'll state it again for the kids out there who might be thinking of reading this because of some pretty heavy allusions to Kafka, it's not about Kafka, nor especially Kafka-esque. </span>

<div id="review_218279931" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/218279931" />
    <a title="Kay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5611008-kay"><img alt="Kay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314169555p2/5611008.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/218279931?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kay" href="/user/show/5611008-kay">Kay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">spiders and roaches and rats, oh my!</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kay by: </span>
      just don't fall down any holes in the laundry room
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5611008-kay?shelf=gods-and-beasts">gods-and-beasts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5611008-kay?shelf=kiddy-lit">kiddy-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5611008-kay?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5611008-kay?shelf=war-and-conflict">war-and-conflict</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer218279931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2581680921374473003"> So, my workplace and a few other firms are a part of this program where we got to a local elementary school to read to kids. I was paired up with a fifth grader who loved to read as much as I did. She blew through Breadcrumbs, which was amazing, and we had just started on Gregor the Overlander (Underland Chronicles, #1) when school was dismissed for summer vacation. Me being my usual ADHD self, I left this book unread for months and months while I pursued other books.Now, after reading the enti</span>
  <span id="freeText2581680921374473003" style="display:none"> So, my workplace and a few other firms are a part of this program where we got to a local elementary school to read to kids. I was paired up with a fifth grader who loved to read as much as I did. She blew through Breadcrumbs, which was amazing, and we had just started on Gregor the Overlander (Underland Chronicles, #1) when school was dismissed for summer vacation. Me being my usual ADHD self, I left this book unread for months and months while I pursued other books.Now, after reading the entire Underland Chronicles in three days, I am so glad I gave this a shot. Plot SummaryGregor is an eleven year old who lives with his mom, grandma, and younger sisters in New York City. His dad disappeared without a word two years ago, and his mom has been struggling to keep the family together since. One day, Gregor and his sister Boots are sucked down a grate in their laundry room, and find themselves in the Underland, a subterranean world populated by white-haired, violet-eyed humans, and oversized cockroaches, spiders, bats and rats. Though all Gregor wants is to go home, he finds himself embroiled in a brewing war between the humans and rats, and perhaps a chance to find his father.My ReactionsThe Underland was interesting, to say the least. I wasn’t too convinced by this subterranean world until about two books in. Maybe it’s because I hatehatehatehatehate rodents and vermin, which is probably not the best attitude to take when living in New York City. Someone once told me about a sighting of a three-foot rat in Brooklyn, and my spidey senses were tingling whenever I entered a subway station for weeks after. (BTW, the antagonists are six-foot tall rats. With their long, ridged tails and sharp teeth.) Kind of like this:Some parts of the book, like the quest and resolution of the prophecy were quite predictable. But like in The Hunger Games has a way of brushing up against the brittleness of the real world without being melodramatic. What remains with me the most was not the questing or the Underland, but Gregor. After his father disappeared, Gregor continually makes sacrifices in the face of hard financial times. Here is an eleven year old who voluntarily gives up summer camp to take care of his baby sister Boots because his mom works nonstop to feed the family. My heart aches for the little guy, who is forced to grow up much too quickly so that the rest of his siblings can enjoy their youths. Not sure how well a fifth grader or even adult could relate--I suppose it depends on the person--but as the oldest in my family, I certainly could.Gregory continues to carry the heavy weight of responsibility with him to the Underland as he takes care of Boots, and that bit of realness threading through the story kept me interested and sympathetic until the end. Overall, I really enjoyed this first book, and the following books are equally (if not more) fun to read. If you thought The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) was a feat in YA lit, Gregor the Overlander is definitely up there in the kid lit world. Both are highly readable for both the younger folk and the adulty folk.3.5 STARS AND HIGHLY RECOMMENDED, especially for younger readers. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2581680921374473003" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2967983393" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2967983393" />
    <a title="Rosaline (Rosaline&#39;s Rolls &amp; Scrolls)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23822042-rosaline-rosaline-s-rolls-scrolls"><img alt="Rosaline (Rosaline&#39;s Rolls &amp; Scrolls)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581593489p2/23822042.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2967983393?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rosaline (Rosaline&#39;s Rolls &amp; Scrolls)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rosaline (Rosaline&#39;s Rolls &amp; Scrolls)" href="/user/show/23822042-rosaline-rosaline-s-rolls-scrolls">Rosaline (Rosaline&#39;s Rolls &amp; Scrolls)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23822042-rosaline-rosaline-s-rolls-scrolls?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23822042-rosaline-rosaline-s-rolls-scrolls?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23822042-rosaline-rosaline-s-rolls-scrolls?shelf=underwhelming">underwhelming</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2967983393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9241861967046467627">Well, what do you know? This was one interesting read!<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/262430.Gregor_the_Overlander__Underland_Chronicles___1_' title='Gregor the Overlander (Underland Chronicles, #1) by Suzanne Collins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gregor the Overlander</a> is about a boy who falls down a <s>rabbit hole</s> and ends up in the Underland, the world under which is filled with giant cockroaches, bats, rats, and humans who immigrated there some centuries ago.<br/>The Underland sounds very interesting, and I was naturally excited to learn more about this cool land of filth. As a kid I've wondered a lot about "what lives beyond the sewers"? But as an adult <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/262430.Gregor_the_Overlander__Underland_Chronicles___1_' title='Gregor the Overlander (Underland Chronicles, #1) by Suzanne Collins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gregor the Overlander</a> lacked a certa</span>
  <span id="freeText9241861967046467627" style="display:none">Well, what do you know? This was one interesting read!<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/262430.Gregor_the_Overlander__Underland_Chronicles___1_" title="Gregor the Overlander (Underland Chronicles, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">Gregor the Overlander</a> is about a boy who falls down a <s>rabbit hole</s> and ends up in the Underland, the world under which is filled with giant cockroaches, bats, rats, and humans who immigrated there some centuries ago.<br />The Underland sounds very interesting, and I was naturally excited to learn more about this cool land of filth. As a kid I've wondered a lot about "what lives beyond the sewers"? But as an adult <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/262430.Gregor_the_Overlander__Underland_Chronicles___1_" title="Gregor the Overlander (Underland Chronicles, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">Gregor the Overlander</a> lacked a certain magic for me. Or as my dear <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29204099-caitlyn" rel="nofollow noopener">Caitlyn</a> would say, it didn't have the "oomph" required for a book to truly wow me. Or at the very least satisfy me.<br /><br /><b>What I liked about the book:</b><br /><br />● The idea of Underland and how it was written in a way that made me actually believe such a thing <i>could</i> happen and such a place <i>could</i> exist. (I kid you not, as I was reading it, I was really feeling like I did as a kid when I truly believed I could travel to Alice's Wonderland if I could just jump down a rabbit hole! )<br />● The book was entertaining and I finished it in one sitting.<br /><br /><b>What I <u>didn't </u>like about the book: </b><br /><br />● The trope of young boy ending up in a magical place and somehow being the chosen one who will bring salvation to an entire population of capable adults.<br />● The trope of the Chosen One never accepting his fate.<br />● The fact that the book was <i>extremely</i> predictable to a point where I felt like I was reading it for the second time. Or the thousands time!<br />● Mr. Chosen One the hero annoyed me to no end with his dumb righteousness and boring inner dialogue. <br />● MC Chosen Pants thoughts in "quotation marks" annoyed me to no end and distracted me from my enjoyment of the book! Can y'all MCs stop thinking like you're talking? You're not having a conversation, you are thinking! This is the one thing I can't stand when reading. Complete laziness and lack of consideration for my sanity. <br /><br />Anyways, overall the book was good enough! It was just not that great. Maybe if I'd read it when I was a child I would've liked it better, but as it was Gregor the Overlander was an entertaining read and I do recommend it to people exploding with underworked imagination in need of something new to devour who also don't mind the points I mentioned.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9241861967046467627" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8205490963067154516">Oh, dear! I've read another children's book, haven't I? Well, if I may be so bold, I liked it a lot more than some of the so-called classics. (I'm so immature, but at least I enjoy myself!)<br/><br/>Though I've never really been one for the 'guy gets sucked into another world' kind of genre, this one put a spin on my thoughts. I've not enjoyed a book so much since... well, a long time. It keeps you in such connection with the characters, despite their being fictional. I especially enjoyed how, as the read</span>
  <span id="freeText8205490963067154516" style="display:none">Oh, dear! I've read another children's book, haven't I? Well, if I may be so bold, I liked it a lot more than some of the so-called classics. (I'm so immature, but at least I enjoy myself!)<br /><br />Though I've never really been one for the 'guy gets sucked into another world' kind of genre, this one put a spin on my thoughts. I've not enjoyed a book so much since... well, a long time. It keeps you in such connection with the characters, despite their being fictional. I especially enjoyed how, as the reader, I had to keep an eye out for it's symbolism- instead of the horribly obvious whack-you-in-the-face kind. <br /><br />I love this book's widespread emotions. And why not? With all that the main characters go through; loss, betrayal, fear for their lives (a lot), war... I'd call it captivating in a very good way.<br /><br /><br />"Ares the flier, I bond to you.<br />Our life and death are one, we two.<br />In dark, in flame, in war, in strife,<br />I save you as I save my life."<br /><br />"Gregor the human, I bond to you.<br />Our life and death are one, we two.<br />In dark, in flame, in war, in strife,<br />I save you as I save my life."<br /></span>

<div id="review_211678142" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/211678142" />
    <a title="Jonathan Terrington" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan-terrington"><img alt="Jonathan Terrington" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478230200p2/6313408.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/211678142?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonathan Terrington" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonathan Terrington" href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan-terrington">Jonathan Terrington</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=children-s-literature">children-s-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=childhood-book">childhood-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer211678142" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2871046314775286301"><br/>Before Suzanne Collins became megafamous from writing about <i>The Hunger Games</i> she wrote a wonderful series of children's books called the <i>Underland Chronicles</i>. These were books that I read as a child and very much enjoyed because of the fascinating fantasy world and ideas. I've always liked the idea of world beyond our own fingers or underneath our feet and that is what Collins decided to tackle in these novels. <br/><br/>The basic premise behind this first book is that of Gregor who stumbles down a laundr</span>
  <span id="freeText2871046314775286301" style="display:none"><br />Before Suzanne Collins became megafamous from writing about <i>The Hunger Games</i> she wrote a wonderful series of children's books called the <i>Underland Chronicles</i>. These were books that I read as a child and very much enjoyed because of the fascinating fantasy world and ideas. I've always liked the idea of world beyond our own fingers or underneath our feet and that is what Collins decided to tackle in these novels. <br /><br />The basic premise behind this first book is that of Gregor who stumbles down a laundry chute in his apartment and ends up in the world beneath our own: the Underland. In this world his father has gone missing and with the aid of gigantic flying bats and strange people Gregor sets off on a quest to find his father and discover more about himself in the process.<br /><br />The inventiveness of this novel, more than the writing (which as I recall was fairly simplistic) is what has stuck with me about this novel. As I come back to write reviews of books I have read in the past, I find it fascinating that of the many hundreds of books (many of which were short pulpy little things) I read in my childhood that I can remember this one very clearly. I can also remember the Moomin books also - if there is any particular correlation I need be concerned with please let me know. Either way I recommend these novels for children to read, or any adults with childlike hearts!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2871046314775286301" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104156012-bryan?shelf=i-would-read-again">i-would-read-again</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3228181387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15801417356526313611">The story takes place in New York City. It is about an 11 year old boy named Gregor. He lives in an apartment with his family. He was sad because he couldn't go to summer camp and had to take care of his grandmother and sister. Gregor had to do the laundry and took his little sister, Boots, with him so that he can watch whatever she does. As Gregor was doing the laundry, Boots sees a ball and goes to it. She then fell into this vent and Gregor was worried and went in with her. Gregor was falling</span>
  <span id="freeText15801417356526313611" style="display:none">The story takes place in New York City. It is about an 11 year old boy named Gregor. He lives in an apartment with his family. He was sad because he couldn't go to summer camp and had to take care of his grandmother and sister. Gregor had to do the laundry and took his little sister, Boots, with him so that he can watch whatever she does. As Gregor was doing the laundry, Boots sees a ball and goes to it. She then fell into this vent and Gregor was worried and went in with her. Gregor was falling in what felt like a bottomless pit and he heard Boots's voice. It was really dark in that pit so he couldn't see Boots. Now he was really worried and he was scared that he would die. Then he suddenly touched the ground and surprisingly survived the fall. He saw Boots holding the ball and he was relieved that she survived too. They walk in this mysterious place and meet some cockroaches which were so big like 5x bigger than the cockroaches they normally saw. The cockroaches offered the "Queen" Boots a ride on his back and Gregor was confused why they called her queen. Then the cockroaches told Gregor to keep up with him and then the cockroach ran very fast that Gregor could barely keep up with him. Then they arrive at this stadium with bats flying around in circle. This is when he meets Queen Luxa which is a very important character in the story. What I liked about the book was how he found out that his father was still alive. I recommend this book to ages 11 and higher. It is a really good book and I really enjoyed reading it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15801417356526313611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4487439622855547777">Already an immensely huge fan of Collins, outstanding series <i>The Huger Games</i>, I just had to see what her other books were like.<br/><br/>Now, I've never been particular pleased with rats and cockroaches to begin with, so having to read about life-sized ones was pretty dame creepy let me tell ya, but never the less, the underground world is fantastically imaginative and unique. <br/>I really enjoyed all the characters, Gregor is a heart felt kid and wonderfully good humored and Boots was to precious for words.<br/><br/>B</span>
  <span id="freeText4487439622855547777" style="display:none">Already an immensely huge fan of Collins, outstanding series <i>The Huger Games</i>, I just had to see what her other books were like.<br /><br />Now, I've never been particular pleased with rats and cockroaches to begin with, so having to read about life-sized ones was pretty dame creepy let me tell ya, but never the less, the underground world is fantastically imaginative and unique. <br />I really enjoyed all the characters, Gregor is a heart felt kid and wonderfully good humored and Boots was to precious for words.<br /><br />Bottom line? I just loved this book. The concept is cool, it's fast paced and suspenseful and I really just enjoyed these characters. Anyone who loves fantasy should have a lot of fun with <b>Gregor the Overlander</b>!<br /><br />Awesome Read!<br />On to book two...;)</span>

<div id="review_667445851" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/667445851" />
    <a title="Kwoomac" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2076898-kwoomac"><img alt="Kwoomac" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333998762p2/2076898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/667445851?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kwoomac" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kwoomac" href="/user/show/2076898-kwoomac">Kwoomac</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=animal-as-main-character">animal-as-main-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=unlikely-hero">unlikely-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=strong-female-protag">strong-female-protag</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=quest">quest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=of-course-i-cried">of-course-i-cried</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer667445851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7087256905803689690">I loved everything about this middle-grade children's book. It is actually Suzanne Collins' very first novel, pre-Hunger Games. It shares a lot with her more famous trilogy. Fast pacing. An ordinary kid forced by extraordinary circumstances into becoming a leader, a hero. Good good guys and bad bad guys. I already mentioned fast pacing. Gregor, an eleven year old boy and his two year old sister Boots get sucked from the laundry room in their NYC apt building into The Underland. The Underland has</span>
  <span id="freeText7087256905803689690" style="display:none">I loved everything about this middle-grade children's book. It is actually Suzanne Collins' very first novel, pre-Hunger Games. It shares a lot with her more famous trilogy. Fast pacing. An ordinary kid forced by extraordinary circumstances into becoming a leader, a hero. Good good guys and bad bad guys. I already mentioned fast pacing. Gregor, an eleven year old boy and his two year old sister Boots get sucked from the laundry room in their NYC apt building into The Underland. The Underland has regular-ish humans, along with giant bats, roaches, rats, and spiders. According to an Underland prophecy, Gregor is the one who will lead them in their battle against the rats. Gregor's only goal is to retrieve his father, who fell down the hole two plus years ago and is now the rats' prisoner. Adventure ensues. <br /><br />There are lots of great characters in the story. The wise elders. The snooty queen-in-training. The giant cockroaches, Tick and Temp. Yes, wonderful, loyal, sweet cockroaches. The giant rat Ripred. is he a spy, a traitor, should they trust him, do they have any choice? I'll never tell.Of course there's Gregor, who learns the obligatory lessons about himself and the world around him. But best of all is Boots. She greets everything in her life with joy. She has no fear. No prejudices. She treats everyone equally, teaching just about everyone a thing or two. Bravo Boots. <br /><br />I'm not sure why I didn't know about this middle-grade series. I loved The Hunger Games. Maybe because the target audience was a little younger there was less hype. All those teen girls who loved The Hunger Games probably think they're a little too old to enjoy this book. It's too bad. I think both boys and girls would love this adrenaline-filled story. Less mushy stuff than Hunger Games, just a straight out quest. It doesn't get any cooler. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7087256905803689690" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1557147711175540544">Brought to you by Suzanne Collins – yes – the same Suzanne Collins that wrote The Hunger Games, Gregor the Overlander is a fun and entertaining read. Geared towards younger audiences, the Gregor books are a kind of Alice in Wonderland for boys.<br/><br/>Eleven year old Gregor is stuck babysitting his baby sister Boots. They are in the basement of their apartment building where Gregor is doing their laundry when Boots disappears into an air duct. Gregor follows Boots and falls into another world. They end </span>
  <span id="freeText1557147711175540544" style="display:none">Brought to you by Suzanne Collins – yes – the same Suzanne Collins that wrote The Hunger Games, Gregor the Overlander is a fun and entertaining read. Geared towards younger audiences, the Gregor books are a kind of Alice in Wonderland for boys.<br /><br />Eleven year old Gregor is stuck babysitting his baby sister Boots. They are in the basement of their apartment building where Gregor is doing their laundry when Boots disappears into an air duct. Gregor follows Boots and falls into another world. They end up in an underground world where cockroaches are really huge – 4 feet tall. And they speak! It is also a world where the humans live in fear of really huge rats and super sized spiders. There are also very large bats. These bats are bonded for life with the humans that live in this world. Cockroaches, rats, spiders, and bats. I think boys would enjoy this.<br /><br />Oh – I forgot – there is a prophecy. (Cue ominous music now…) <br /><br />Overall, a fun and exciting read perfect for the young and possibly reluctant reader in your life. My boys can’t wait to get their hands on this book. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14244354170404354996">My 10-yr old son moped around for days after he finished this series because he was so bummed there were no more books left to read. I decided I needed to see for myself what all the fuss was about, and I was also intrigued to see Suzanne Collins' work prior to The Hunger Games. I wasn't disappointed! It is geared towards a younger crowd than Hunger Games, but was still enjoyable for me as an adult. What I really loved is that it has at its core a functional family. Gregor is the hero, but he st</span>
  <span id="freeText14244354170404354996" style="display:none">My 10-yr old son moped around for days after he finished this series because he was so bummed there were no more books left to read. I decided I needed to see for myself what all the fuss was about, and I was also intrigued to see Suzanne Collins' work prior to The Hunger Games. I wasn't disappointed! It is geared towards a younger crowd than Hunger Games, but was still enjoyable for me as an adult. What I really loved is that it has at its core a functional family. Gregor is the hero, but he still has a mom and dad he looks up to, as well as younger siblings he cares for. Hurray for a good fantasy/adventure with great values!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1430030587?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Filipa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Filipa" href="/user/show/10622600-filipa">Filipa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1430030587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7381085172865709782">aww~~ guys !<br/>I really liked this book!<br/><br/>It's a story about adventures on unknown worlds, about family and love.<br/>At first was really weird, reading about a place where bats, cockroaches, spiders, rats, and all those creepy disgusting things, are part of the "society". <br/>They think, they talk, they feel.. well, I'm not exactly looking forward to have a giant cockroach in front of me.. but you'll get used to picture it throughout the book I guess.<br/><br/>Gregor is a great main character and I really loved Boots.</span>
  <span id="freeText7381085172865709782" style="display:none">aww~~ guys !<br />I really liked this book!<br /><br />It's a story about adventures on unknown worlds, about family and love.<br />At first was really weird, reading about a place where bats, cockroaches, spiders, rats, and all those creepy disgusting things, are part of the "society". <br />They think, they talk, they feel.. well, I'm not exactly looking forward to have a giant cockroach in front of me.. but you'll get used to picture it throughout the book I guess.<br /><br />Gregor is a great main character and I really loved Boots. She was so essential in all scenes, and the way Gregor looks out for her is so right. Also the innocence of childhood, all the trust and love she shows to everyone, is such a nice reminder to treat everyone equally.<br /><br />The central dogma was also pretty good, finding Gregor's father and the several steps they had to perform to get to the end of their quest and all the twists and turns, really got me entertained, focused and attached there.<br />It really felt like a children's book at first but the more I read the more not childish looked to me.<br /><br />And gosh, I cried for the death of a cockroach!<br />I guess that says alot about Suzanne's writing. She's indeed phenomenal story teller. And I had a really great, short (cuz the book is pretty small ~fast read YEY~), time reading it and I really want to read the other books in this series.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7381085172865709782" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catherine" href="/user/show/867628-catherine">Catherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/867628-catherine?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/867628-catherine?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/867628-catherine?shelf=middle-grades">middle-grades</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/867628-catherine?shelf=fantastical">fantastical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/867628-catherine?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/867628-catherine?shelf=read-more-than-once">read-more-than-once</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/867628-catherine?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/867628-catherine?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer254690161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13610253739523752627">Although it's been many years since I read it, this book most reminded me of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18131.A_Wrinkle_in_Time__Time_Quintet___1_' title='A Wrinkle in Time (Time Quintet, #1) by Madeleine L'Engle' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Wrinkle in Time</a>. Both books concern a family with a missing scientist father (Gregor's father is a Science teacher), but instead of exploring space, Gregor and his toddler sister fall down a chute into a world beneath our own. This world is inhabited by giant bats, rats, spiders, and cockroaches, as well as humans who have lived below ground for many generations. Gregor just wants to get back home, but the Underlander</span>
  <span id="freeText13610253739523752627" style="display:none">Although it's been many years since I read it, this book most reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18131.A_Wrinkle_in_Time__Time_Quintet___1_" title="A Wrinkle in Time (Time Quintet, #1) by Madeleine L'Engle" rel="nofollow noopener">A Wrinkle in Time</a>. Both books concern a family with a missing scientist father (Gregor's father is a Science teacher), but instead of exploring space, Gregor and his toddler sister fall down a chute into a world beneath our own. This world is inhabited by giant bats, rats, spiders, and cockroaches, as well as humans who have lived below ground for many generations. Gregor just wants to get back home, but the Underlanders are convinced he is the hero from an old prophecy and that his father is being held captive elsewhere underground. <br /><br />I picked up this book because it was the first novel written by the author now famous for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a>. This series is written for a younger audience, and although I suppose both civilizations (Panem &amp; Underland) could be considered dystopias, Underland is a fantasy land beneath our own contemporary world. <br /><br />Gregor is a likeable character, but my favorite is his little sister "Boots" (actual name Margaret). She's a feisty, fearless little two-year-old who is portrayed very realistically, dialogue, tantrums &amp; all. <br /><br />I really don't understand why I haven't heard of this series before, since I think it's fantastic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13610253739523752627" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
